<div class="ltx_abstract">
<h6 class="ltx_title ltx_title_abstract">Abstract</h6>
<p class="ltx_p" id="id5.2">Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG) has recently emerged as a promising solution to alleviate Large Language Model (LLM)’s deficiency in lack of knowledge. Existing RAG datasets, however, do not adequately represent the diverse and dynamic nature of real-world Question Answering (QA) tasks. To bridge this gap, we introduce the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="id5.2.1">Comprehensive RAG Benchmark (CRAG)</span>, a factual question answering benchmark of 4,409 question-answer pairs and mock APIs to simulate web and Knowledge Graph (KG) search. CRAG is designed to encapsulate a diverse array of questions across five domains and eight question categories, reflecting varied entity popularity from popular to long-tail, and temporal dynamisms ranging from years to seconds.
Our evaluation of this benchmark highlights the gap to fully trustworthy QA. Whereas most advanced LLMs achieve <math alttext="\leq 34\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="id4.1.m1.1"><semantics id="id4.1.m1.1a"><mrow id="id4.1.m1.1.1" xref="id4.1.m1.1.1.cmml"><mi id="id4.1.m1.1.1.2" xref="id4.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml"></mi><mo id="id4.1.m1.1.1.1" xref="id4.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml">≤</mo><mrow id="id4.1.m1.1.1.3" xref="id4.1.m1.1.1.3.cmml"><mn id="id4.1.m1.1.1.3.2" xref="id4.1.m1.1.1.3.2.cmml">34</mn><mo id="id4.1.m1.1.1.3.1" xref="id4.1.m1.1.1.3.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="id4.1.m1.1b"><apply id="id4.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="id4.1.m1.1.1"><leq id="id4.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="id4.1.m1.1.1.1"></leq><csymbol cd="latexml" id="id4.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml" xref="id4.1.m1.1.1.2">absent</csymbol><apply id="id4.1.m1.1.1.3.cmml" xref="id4.1.m1.1.1.3"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="id4.1.m1.1.1.3.1.cmml" xref="id4.1.m1.1.1.3.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="id4.1.m1.1.1.3.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="id4.1.m1.1.1.3.2">34</cn></apply></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="id4.1.m1.1c">\leq 34\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="id4.1.m1.1d">≤ 34 %</annotation></semantics></math> accuracy on CRAG, adding RAG in a straightforward manner improves the accuracy only to 44%. State-of-the-art industry RAG solutions only answer <math alttext="63\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="id5.2.m2.1"><semantics id="id5.2.m2.1a"><mrow id="id5.2.m2.1.1" xref="id5.2.m2.1.1.cmml"><mn id="id5.2.m2.1.1.2" xref="id5.2.m2.1.1.2.cmml">63</mn><mo id="id5.2.m2.1.1.1" xref="id5.2.m2.1.1.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="id5.2.m2.1b"><apply id="id5.2.m2.1.1.cmml" xref="id5.2.m2.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="id5.2.m2.1.1.1.cmml" xref="id5.2.m2.1.1.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="id5.2.m2.1.1.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="id5.2.m2.1.1.2">63</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="id5.2.m2.1c">63\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="id5.2.m2.1d">63 %</annotation></semantics></math> of questions without any hallucination.
CRAG also reveals much lower accuracy in answering questions regarding facts with higher dynamism, lower popularity, or higher complexity, suggesting future research directions.
The CRAG benchmark laid the groundwork for a KDD Cup 2024 challenge and attracted thousands of participants and submissions. We commit to maintaining CRAG to serve research communities in advancing RAG solutions and general QA solutions. <span class="ltx_text" id="id5.2.2" style="color:#000000;">CRAG is available at <a class="ltx_ref ltx_url ltx_font_typewriter" href="https://github.com/facebookresearch/CRAG/" title="">https://github.com/facebookresearch/CRAG/</a>.</span></p>
</div>
<section class="ltx_section ltx_pruned_first" id="S1">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">1 </span>Introduction</h2>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.p1.1">Large Language Models (LLMs) have transformed the landscape of Natural Language Processing (NLP) tasks, especially in Question Answering (QA) <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib38" title="">38</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib22" title="">22</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib20" title="">20</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib39" title="">39</a>]</cite>.
Despite the advancements, the issue of hallucination persists as a significant challenge; LLMs may generate answers that lack factual accuracy or grounding <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib27" title="">27</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib14" title="">14</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib30" title="">30</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib32" title="">32</a>]</cite>. Studies have shown that GPT-4’s accuracy in answering questions referring to slow-changing or fast-changing facts is below 15% <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib36" title="">36</a>]</cite>; even for stable (never-changing) facts, GPT-4’s accuracy in answering questions referring to torso-to-tail (less popular) entities is below 35% <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib29" title="">29</a>]</cite>. Overcoming hallucinations thus becomes a priority in building reliable QA systems <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib14" title="">14</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib13" title="">13</a>]</cite>.</p>
</div>
<figure class="ltx_figure" id="S1.F1"><img alt="Refer to caption" class="ltx_graphics ltx_centering ltx_img_landscape" height="173" id="S1.F1.g1" src="x1.png" width="681"/>
<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure">Figure 1: </span>QA using LLMs (a) without RAG vs. (b) with RAG.</figcaption>
</figure>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.p2.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p2.1.1">Retrieval-Augmented Generation (RAG)</span> <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib12" title="">12</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib19" title="">19</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib6" title="">6</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib8" title="">8</a>]</cite> has recently emerged as a promising solution to alleviate LLM’s deficiency in lack of knowledge and attracted a lot of attention from both academia research and industry. Given a question, a RAG system searches external sources to retrieve relevant information and then provides grounded answers <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib12" title="">12</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib19" title="">19</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib7" title="">7</a>]</cite> (see Figure <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S1.F1" title="Figure 1 ‣ 1 Introduction ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1</span></a> for an illustration). Despite its potential, RAG still faces many challenges, such as selecting the most relevant information, reducing question answering latency, and synthesizing information to answer complex questions.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.p3.1">A comprehensive benchmark is currently missing to advance continued research efforts in this field.
Our goal is to build a benchmark that can provide a holistic view of the important capabilities and fast but reliable evaluation for RAG to propel the area forward. What is a good benchmark for QA over LLMs? We consider five critical features.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.p4">
<ol class="ltx_enumerate" id="S1.I1">
<li class="ltx_item" id="S1.I1.i1" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">1.</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="S1.I1.i1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.I1.i1.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S1.I1.i1.p1.1.1">Realism:</span> First and foremost, a good benchmark shall best reflect real use cases. In other words, a solution that achieves high metrics in the benchmark shall also perform very well in real scenarios. For example, the questions in a RAG benchmark shall be similar to questions people ask in real-world QA scenarios.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="S1.I1.i2" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">2.</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="S1.I1.i2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.I1.i2.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S1.I1.i2.p1.1.1">Richness:</span> The benchmark shall contain a diverse set of instance types, covering both common use cases and some complex and advanced use cases, to represent real-world challenges and reveal possible limitations of existing solutions.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="S1.I1.i3" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">3.</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="S1.I1.i3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.I1.i3.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S1.I1.i3.p1.1.1">Insightfulness:</span> The benchmark shall allow for an easy understanding of performance on different slices of the data, reflecting the capability of the solution in addressing different types of challenges.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="S1.I1.i4" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">4.</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="S1.I1.i4.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.I1.i4.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S1.I1.i4.p1.1.1">Reliability:</span> The benchmark shall allow reliable assessment of metrics: the ground truths shall be accurate; the metrics shall well capture the performance of the model; the evaluation shall be easy and reliable, and the computed metrics shall hold statistical significance.</p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="S1.I1.i5" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">5.</span>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.I1.i5.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.I1.i5.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S1.I1.i5.p1.1.1">Longevity:</span> Finally, to enable research and experimental comparison in a long term, the scenarios and the data in the benchmark shall not quickly expire and ideally shall be refreshed and improved over time.</p>
</div>
</li>
</ol>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.p5">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.p5.1">We strive to create a benchmark that have all of the aforementioned features, and we call it <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p5.1.1">CRAG – Comprehensive benchmark for RAG</span>. Our work makes three contributions.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.p6">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.p6.1">Our first contribution is the dataset itself (Section <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S3" title="3 Dataset Description ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">3</span></a>). CRAG contains a <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.1">rich</span> set of 4,409 QA pairs from five domains: <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.2">Finance, Sports, Music, Movie,</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.3">Open domain</span>. In addition to simple-fact questions (asking for an attribute of an entity), CRAG contains seven types of complex questions to cover real user queries: questions with <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.4">Conditions</span>, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.5">Comparison</span> questions, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.6">Aggregation</span> questions, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.7">Multi-hop</span> questions, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.8">Set queries</span>, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.9">Post-processing-heavy</span> questions, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.10">False-premise</span> questions. CRAG reflects varied entity popularity from popular to long-tail and temporal spans ranging from seconds to years, allowing easy deep dives for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.11">insights</span>. As we generated the questions, we referred to smart assistant use cases to make sure the questions are <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.12">realistic</span>, paraphrased the questions to increase the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.13">diversity</span> of expressions, and manually verified ground truths to ensure <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p6.1.14">reliability</span>.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.p7">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.p7.1">In addition to QA pairs, CRAG provides mock APIs to simulate retrieval from a diverse range of available information.
This includes up to 50 full HTML pages for each question returned from a real-world search engine—the Brave Search API <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib5" title="">5</a>]</cite>, and mock KGs with 2.6 million entities. For the mock KGs, we deliberately make sure that the retrieval candidates reflect noises in a <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p7.1.1">realistic</span> setting.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.p8">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.p8.1">Our second contribution is the evaluation mechanism to allow for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p8.1.1">reliable</span> comparisons. We designed 3 tasks to test different components in RAG solutions: <span class="ltx_text" id="S1.p8.1.2" style="color:#000000;">retrieval summarization, knowledge graph and web retrieval, and end-to-end retrieval-augmented generation</span> (Section <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S2" title="2 Problem Description ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2</span></a>). Instead of computing the percentage of correctly answered questions, our score system distinguishes hallucinated answers and missing answers, and gives the former a higher penalty as it can be more harmful to ruin user trust. We also design an effective automatic evaluation mechanism to allow for fast evaluations and iterations (Section <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S4" title="4 Metrics and Evaluation ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">4</span></a>).</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.p9">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.p9.2">Our third contribution is a comprehensive evaluation of straightforward RAG solutions and industry state-of-the-art solutions on RAG (Section <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S5" title="5 Benchmarking ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">5</span></a>). Whereas most advanced LLMs achieve <math alttext="\leq 34\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S1.p9.1.m1.1"><semantics id="S1.p9.1.m1.1a"><mrow id="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1" xref="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.cmml"><mi id="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.2" xref="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml"></mi><mo id="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.1" xref="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml">≤</mo><mrow id="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.3" xref="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.3.cmml"><mn id="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.3.2" xref="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.3.2.cmml">34</mn><mo id="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.3.1" xref="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.3.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S1.p9.1.m1.1b"><apply id="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1"><leq id="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.1"></leq><csymbol cd="latexml" id="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml" xref="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.2">absent</csymbol><apply id="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.3.cmml" xref="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.3"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.3.1.cmml" xref="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.3.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.3.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S1.p9.1.m1.1.1.3.2">34</cn></apply></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S1.p9.1.m1.1c">\leq 34\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S1.p9.1.m1.1d">≤ 34 %</annotation></semantics></math> accuracy on CRAG, adding RAG in a straightforward manner improves the accuracy only to 44%. State-of-the-art industry RAG solutions answer only <math alttext="63\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S1.p9.2.m2.1"><semantics id="S1.p9.2.m2.1a"><mrow id="S1.p9.2.m2.1.1" xref="S1.p9.2.m2.1.1.cmml"><mn id="S1.p9.2.m2.1.1.2" xref="S1.p9.2.m2.1.1.2.cmml">63</mn><mo id="S1.p9.2.m2.1.1.1" xref="S1.p9.2.m2.1.1.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S1.p9.2.m2.1b"><apply id="S1.p9.2.m2.1.1.cmml" xref="S1.p9.2.m2.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="S1.p9.2.m2.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S1.p9.2.m2.1.1.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="S1.p9.2.m2.1.1.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S1.p9.2.m2.1.1.2">63</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S1.p9.2.m2.1c">63\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S1.p9.2.m2.1d">63 %</annotation></semantics></math> questions without any hallucination, still having much lower accuracy in answering questions regarding facts with higher dynamism, lower popularity, or higher complexity. These evaluations serve two roles: first, they demonstrate that CRAG has appropriate level of difficulty and allows insights drawn from different dimensions of diversities the benchmark has incorporated; second, they highlight the gaps and research directions to a fully trustworthy QA system.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.p10">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.p10.1">The CRAG benchmark laid the groundwork for a KDD Cup 2024 challenge<span class="ltx_note ltx_role_footnote" id="footnote1"><sup class="ltx_note_mark">1</sup><span class="ltx_note_outer"><span class="ltx_note_content"><sup class="ltx_note_mark">1</sup><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_note">1</span><a class="ltx_ref ltx_url ltx_font_typewriter" href="https://www.aicrowd.com/challenges/meta-comprehensive-rag-benchmark-kdd-cup-2024" title="">https://www.aicrowd.com/challenges/meta-comprehensive-rag-benchmark-kdd-cup-2024</a></span></span></span>, has attracted thousands of participants and submissions within the first 50 days of the competition. We commit to maintaining CRAG to serve research communities in advancing RAG solutions and general QA solutions.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.p11">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.p11.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S1.p11.1.1">Comparison with existing benchmarks.</span>
Table <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S1.T1" title="Table 1 ‣ 1 Introduction ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1</span></a> compares CRAG with existing benchmarks for factual question answering.
Traditional QA benchmarks such as Natural Questions (NQ) <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib18" title="">18</a>]</cite>, TriviaQA <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib16" title="">16</a>]</cite>, MS MARCO <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib4" title="">4</a>]</cite>, and QALD-10 <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib35" title="">35</a>]</cite> have advanced QA in the past decade but <span class="ltx_text" id="S1.p11.1.2" style="color:#000000;">consider only web retrieved <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p11.1.2.1">or</span> KG retrieved contents, and</span> do <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S1.p11.1.3">not</span> adequately represent the diverse and dynamic challenges that RAG is facing. New benchmarks for LLM or RAG usually target certain capabilities of the QA system. <span class="ltx_text" id="S1.p11.1.4" style="color:#000000;">Researchers created benchmarks to evaluate how well the systems can answer simple knowledge questions <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib29" title="">29</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib30" title="">30</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib23" title="">23</a>]</cite> and handle more advanced scenarios. These include answering questions with changing answers <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib36" title="">36</a>]</cite>, integrating information from multiple documents <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib6" title="">6</a>]</cite>, addressing multi-hop questions <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib33" title="">33</a>]</cite>, and answering questions with long texts <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib26" title="">26</a>]</cite>. Moreover, traditional QA benchmarks usually adopt matching-based metrics such as ROUGE <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib21" title="">21</a>]</cite> or F1 to evaluate the quality of the responses <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib18" title="">18</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib16" title="">16</a>]</cite>. These metrics, although working well for extractive methods, are known to not perform very effectively for LLMs that generate free-form responses <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib11" title="">11</a>]</cite>.</span></p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S1.p12">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S1.p12.1"><span class="ltx_text" id="S1.p12.1.1" style="color:#000000;">Despite CRAG being smaller than MS MARCO and NQ</span>, it offers several distinctive advantages:
comprehensive coverage, realistic testing with mock APIs, dynamic question handling, diverse fact popularity, extensive content beyond Wikipedia, <span class="ltx_text" id="S1.p12.1.2" style="color:#000000;">and fast yet reliable evaluation.</span>
These features make CRAG a robust and versatile benchmark for testing RAG systems and broadly QA systems, providing a shared testbed to evaluate how these systems handle real-world, dynamic, and diverse information retrieval and synthesis challenges for reliable LLM-based question answering.</p>
</div>

<span class="ltx_tr" id="S1.T1.1.1.5.2.1.2">

<span class="ltx_tabular ltx_align_middle" id="S1.T1.1.1.6.2.1">
<span class="ltx_tr" id="S1.T1.1.1.6.2.1.1">

<section class="ltx_section" id="S2">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">2 </span>Problem Description</h2>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S2.p1.2">A RAG QA system takes a question <math alttext="Q" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S2.p1.1.m1.1"><semantics id="S2.p1.1.m1.1a"><mi id="S2.p1.1.m1.1.1" xref="S2.p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml">Q</mi><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S2.p1.1.m1.1b"><ci id="S2.p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="S2.p1.1.m1.1.1">𝑄</ci></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S2.p1.1.m1.1c">Q</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S2.p1.1.m1.1d">italic_Q</annotation></semantics></math> as input and outputs an answer <math alttext="A" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S2.p1.2.m2.1"><semantics id="S2.p1.2.m2.1a"><mi id="S2.p1.2.m2.1.1" xref="S2.p1.2.m2.1.1.cmml">A</mi><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S2.p1.2.m2.1b"><ci id="S2.p1.2.m2.1.1.cmml" xref="S2.p1.2.m2.1.1">𝐴</ci></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S2.p1.2.m2.1c">A</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S2.p1.2.m2.1d">italic_A</annotation></semantics></math>; the answer is generated by LLMs according to information retrieved from external sources or directly from the knowledge internalized in the model. The answer should provide useful information to answer the question without adding any hallucination.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S2.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S2.p2.1">We designed three tasks. They share the same set of (question, answer) pairs but differ in the external data accessible for retrieval to augment QA.
Here, we provide the content that can be leveraged in QA to ensure fair comparisons. We describe how we generated the data in Section <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S3" title="3 Dataset Description ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">3</span></a>.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S2.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S2.p3.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S2.p3.1.1">Task 1: Retrieval Summarization.</span> In Task 1, we provide up to five web pages for each question. These web pages are likely, but not guaranteed, to be relevant to the question. This task aims to test the answer generation capability of a RAG system.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S2.p4">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S2.p4.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S2.p4.1.1">Task 2: KG and Web Retrieval Augmentation.</span> In Task 2, we in addition provide <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S2.p4.1.2">mock APIs</span> to access information from underlying <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S2.p4.1.3">mock KGs</span>. The mock KGs store structured data relevant to the questions; answers to the questions may or may not exist in the mock KGs. The mock APIs take input parameters, oftentimes parsed from the question, and provide structured data from the mocked KGs to support answer generation. This task tests how well a RAG system 1) queries structured data sources and 2) synthesizes information from different sources.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S2.p5">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S2.p5.2"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S2.p5.2.1">Task 3: End-to-end RAG.</span> Similar to Task 2, Task 3 also provides both web search results and mock APIs as candidates for retrieval but provides <math alttext="50" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S2.p5.1.m1.1"><semantics id="S2.p5.1.m1.1a"><mn id="S2.p5.1.m1.1.1" xref="S2.p5.1.m1.1.1.cmml">50</mn><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S2.p5.1.m1.1b"><cn id="S2.p5.1.m1.1.1.cmml" type="integer" xref="S2.p5.1.m1.1.1">50</cn></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S2.p5.1.m1.1c">50</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S2.p5.1.m1.1d">50</annotation></semantics></math> web pages, instead of <math alttext="5" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S2.p5.2.m2.1"><semantics id="S2.p5.2.m2.1a"><mn id="S2.p5.2.m2.1.1" xref="S2.p5.2.m2.1.1.cmml">5</mn><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S2.p5.2.m2.1b"><cn id="S2.p5.2.m2.1.1.cmml" type="integer" xref="S2.p5.2.m2.1.1">5</cn></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S2.p5.2.m2.1c">5</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S2.p5.2.m2.1d">5</annotation></semantics></math>, as candidates. The larger set of web pages are more likely to provide necessary information to answer the question, but meanwhile are more likely to contain noises. As such, Task 3 in addition tests how a RAG system ranks a larger number of retrieval results.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S2.p6">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S2.p6.1">The three tasks, each adding upon the previous one, allow testing different capabilities of the RAG systems. <span class="ltx_text" id="S2.p6.1.1" style="color:#000000;">The only component of a RAG system not covered by these tasks is search retrieval. One may easily extend the tasks to use all 220K webpages in our benchmark as the search corpus for fully end-to-end testing.</span></p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_section" id="S3">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">3 </span>Dataset Description</h2>
<figure class="ltx_table" id="S3.T2">
<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_table">Table 2: </span>Definition of CRAG question types.</figcaption>
<table class="ltx_tabular ltx_centering ltx_align_middle" id="S3.T2.1">
<tr class="ltx_tr" id="S3.T2.1.1">
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_tt" id="S3.T2.1.1.1">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.1.1.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.1.1.1.1" style="width:74.0pt;"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S3.T2.1.1.1.1.1.1">Question type</span></span>
</span>
</td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_tt" id="S3.T2.1.1.2">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.1.2.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.1.2.1.1" style="width:298.8pt;"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S3.T2.1.1.2.1.1.1">Definition</span></span>
</span>
</td>
</tr>
<tr class="ltx_tr" id="S3.T2.1.2">
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.2.1">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.2.1.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.2.1.1.1" style="width:74.0pt;">Simple</span>
</span>
</td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.2.2">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.2.2.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.2.2.1.1" style="width:298.8pt;">Questions asking for simple facts that are unlikely to change overtime, such as the birth date of a person and the authors of a book.</span>
</span>
</td>
</tr>
<tr class="ltx_tr" id="S3.T2.1.3">
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.3.1">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.3.1.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.3.1.1.1" style="width:74.0pt;">Simple w. Condition</span>
</span>
</td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.3.2">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.3.2.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.3.2.1.1" style="width:298.8pt;">Questions asking for simple facts with some given conditions, such as stock prices on a certain date and a director’s recent movies in a certain genre.</span>
</span>
</td>
</tr>
<tr class="ltx_tr" id="S3.T2.1.4">
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.4.1">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.4.1.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.4.1.1.1" style="width:74.0pt;">Set</span>
</span>
</td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.4.2">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.4.2.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.4.2.1.1" style="width:298.8pt;">Questions that expect a set of entities or objects as the answer (e.g., “<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.T2.1.4.2.1.1.1">what are the continents in the southern hemisphere?</span>”).</span>
</span>
</td>
</tr>
<tr class="ltx_tr" id="S3.T2.1.5">
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.5.1">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.5.1.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.5.1.1.1" style="width:74.0pt;">Comparison</span>
</span>
</td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.5.2">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.5.2.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.5.2.1.1" style="width:298.8pt;">Questions that compare two entities (e.g., “<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.T2.1.5.2.1.1.1">who started performing earlier, Adele or Ed Sheeran?</span>”).</span>
</span>
</td>
</tr>
<tr class="ltx_tr" id="S3.T2.1.6">
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.6.1">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.6.1.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.6.1.1.1" style="width:74.0pt;">Aggregation</span>
</span>
</td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.6.2">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.6.2.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.6.2.1.1" style="width:298.8pt;">Questions that require aggregation of retrieval results to answer (e.g., “<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.T2.1.6.2.1.1.1">how many Oscar awards did Meryl Streep win?</span>”).</span>
</span>
</td>
</tr>
<tr class="ltx_tr" id="S3.T2.1.7">
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.7.1">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.7.1.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.7.1.1.1" style="width:74.0pt;">Multi-hop</span>
</span>
</td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.7.2">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.7.2.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.7.2.1.1" style="width:298.8pt;">Questions that require chaining multiple pieces of information to compose the answer (e.g., “<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.T2.1.7.2.1.1.1">who acted in Ang Lee’s latest movie?</span>”).</span>
</span>
</td>
</tr>
<tr class="ltx_tr" id="S3.T2.1.8">
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.8.1">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.8.1.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.8.1.1.1" style="width:74.0pt;">Post-processing-heavy</span>
</span>
</td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.8.2">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.8.2.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.8.2.1.1" style="width:298.8pt;">Questions that need reasoning or processing of the retrieved information to obtain the answer (e.g., “<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.T2.1.8.2.1.1.1">how many days did Thurgood Marshall serve as a Supreme Court justice?</span>”).</span>
</span>
</td>
</tr>
<tr class="ltx_tr" id="S3.T2.1.9">
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_bb ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.9.1">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.9.1.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.9.1.1.1" style="width:74.0pt;">False Premise</span>
</span>
</td>
<td class="ltx_td ltx_align_justify ltx_align_top ltx_border_bb ltx_border_t" id="S3.T2.1.9.2">
<span class="ltx_inline-block ltx_align_top" id="S3.T2.1.9.2.1">
<span class="ltx_p" id="S3.T2.1.9.2.1.1" style="width:298.8pt;">Questions that have a false preposition or assumption (e.g., “<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.T2.1.9.2.1.1.1">What’s the name of Taylor Swift’s rap album before she transitioned to pop?</span>” (Taylor Swift has not yet released any rap album)).</span>
</span>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</figure>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.p1.1">CRAG contains two parts of data: the QA pairs and the contents for retrieval. We now describe each part of the data. Data generation details can be found in Appendix <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS1.SSS1" title="A.1.1 Constructing QA pairs from KGs ‣ A.1 Dataset ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.1.1</span></a>–<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS1.SSS6" title="A.1.6 The mock data and mock APIs ‣ A.1 Dataset ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.1.6</span></a>.</p>
</div>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="S3.SS1">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">3.1 </span>Question answering pairs</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.SS1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.SS1.p1.1">CRAG covers five domains: Finance, Sports, Music, Movie, and Open domain, and eight types of questions, all in English. The question types are listed in Table <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S3.T2" title="Table 2 ‣ 3 Dataset Description ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2</span></a>. We constructed the question-answer pairs both from underlying KGs and web contents.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.SS1.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.SS1.p2.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S3.SS1.p2.1.1">QA pairs constructed from KGs.</span>

We constructed QA pairs from KGs by collecting a set of entities based on publicly available data and then creating 600+ question templates based on selected entity types and relations. Next, we sampled entities with different popularities (head, torso and tail) following <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib29" title="">29</a>]</cite> from the KGs to fill in the templates and generate the full question and answer.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.SS1.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.SS1.p3.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S3.SS1.p3.1.1">QA pairs constructed from web contents.</span>
We asked annotators to write down possible questions that users may ask (e.g., “<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.SS1.p3.1.2">most popular action movies in 2023</span>”) and created QA pairs from the corresponding web search results.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.SS1.p4">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.SS1.p4.4">Using the above methods, we collected 2,425 <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.1">Web Questions</span> and 1,984 <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.2">KG Questions</span>, with <math alttext="661" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S3.SS1.p4.1.m1.1"><semantics id="S3.SS1.p4.1.m1.1a"><mn id="S3.SS1.p4.1.m1.1.1" xref="S3.SS1.p4.1.m1.1.1.cmml">661</mn><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S3.SS1.p4.1.m1.1b"><cn id="S3.SS1.p4.1.m1.1.1.cmml" type="integer" xref="S3.SS1.p4.1.m1.1.1">661</cn></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S3.SS1.p4.1.m1.1c">661</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S3.SS1.p4.1.m1.1d">661</annotation></semantics></math>, <math alttext="658" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S3.SS1.p4.2.m2.1"><semantics id="S3.SS1.p4.2.m2.1a"><mn id="S3.SS1.p4.2.m2.1.1" xref="S3.SS1.p4.2.m2.1.1.cmml">658</mn><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S3.SS1.p4.2.m2.1b"><cn id="S3.SS1.p4.2.m2.1.1.cmml" type="integer" xref="S3.SS1.p4.2.m2.1.1">658</cn></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S3.SS1.p4.2.m2.1c">658</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S3.SS1.p4.2.m2.1d">658</annotation></semantics></math>, and <math alttext="665" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S3.SS1.p4.3.m3.1"><semantics id="S3.SS1.p4.3.m3.1a"><mn id="S3.SS1.p4.3.m3.1.1" xref="S3.SS1.p4.3.m3.1.1.cmml">665</mn><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S3.SS1.p4.3.m3.1b"><cn id="S3.SS1.p4.3.m3.1.1.cmml" type="integer" xref="S3.SS1.p4.3.m3.1.1">665</cn></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S3.SS1.p4.3.m3.1c">665</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S3.SS1.p4.3.m3.1d">665</annotation></semantics></math> <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.3">KG Questions</span> containing <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.4">head</span>, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.5">torso</span>, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.6">tail</span> entities respectively. Tables <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S3.T3" title="Table 3 ‣ 3.1 Question answering pairs ‣ 3 Dataset Description ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">3</span></a> and <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S3.T4" title="Table 4 ‣ 3.1 Question answering pairs ‣ 3 Dataset Description ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">4</span></a> summarize the distribution of the questions across different dimensions. The size of each dimension slice (e.g., fast-changing facts) allows us to get metrics with <math alttext="&lt;5\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1"><semantics id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1a"><mrow id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1" xref="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.cmml"><mi id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.2" xref="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.2.cmml"></mi><mo id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.1" xref="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.1.cmml">&lt;</mo><mrow id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.3" xref="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.3.cmml"><mn id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.3.2" xref="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.3.2.cmml">5</mn><mo id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.3.1" xref="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.3.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1b"><apply id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.cmml" xref="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1"><lt id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.1"></lt><csymbol cd="latexml" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.2.cmml" xref="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.2">absent</csymbol><apply id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.3.cmml" xref="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.3"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.3.1.cmml" xref="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.3.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.3.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1.1.3.2">5</cn></apply></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1c">&lt;5\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.m4.1d">&lt; 5 %</annotation></semantics></math> margin-of-error (with 95% confidence level) for most of the cases. The dynamism distribution roughly reflects the nature of the domain (e.g., much more real-time questions for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.SS1.p4.4.7">Finance</span> than for other domains). See Appendix <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS1.SSS2" title="A.1.2 Definition of dynamism categories ‣ A.1 Dataset ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.1.2</span></a> for the definition of the dynamism categories.</p>
</div>

</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="S3.SS2">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">3.2 </span>Contents for retrieval</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.SS2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.SS2.p1.1">We included two types of contents for retrieval to simulate the practical scenario for RAG: web search and KG search.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.SS2.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.SS2.p2.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S3.SS2.p2.1.1">Web search results.</span>

For each question, we used the question text as the search query and stored up to <math alttext="50" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S3.SS2.p2.1.m1.1"><semantics id="S3.SS2.p2.1.m1.1a"><mn id="S3.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1" xref="S3.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.cmml">50</mn><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S3.SS2.p2.1.m1.1b"><cn id="S3.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.cmml" type="integer" xref="S3.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1">50</cn></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S3.SS2.p2.1.m1.1c">50</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S3.SS2.p2.1.m1.1d">50</annotation></semantics></math> HTML pages from the Brave search API <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib5" title="">5</a>]</cite>. See Table <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.T8" title="Table 8 ‣ A.1.5 An example of retrieved web search results ‣ A.1 Dataset ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">8</span></a> in Appendix <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS1.SSS5" title="A.1.5 An example of retrieved web search results ‣ A.1 Dataset ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.1.5</span></a> for an example.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.SS2.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.SS2.p3.1"><span class="ltx_text" id="S3.SS2.p3.1.1" style="color:#000000;">We estimated the web search recall with a heuristic-based method: first check whether the ground truth answer URL was found among the pages; if not, decide whether the fact in the ground truths is contained in the page snippet or content with an LLM. In particular, we pass the question, ground truth, and the pages to Llama 3 70B Instruct and ask it to judge if the context is sufficient to answer the question. </span></p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.SS2.p4">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.SS2.p4.2"><span class="ltx_text" id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2" style="color:#000000;">Figure <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S3.F2" title="Figure 2 ‣ 3.2 Contents for retrieval ‣ 3 Dataset Description ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2</span></a> shows the estimated web search recall curve for all CRAG questions, with an overall recall of 85% when using all 50 pages.
It reflects multiple advantages of the benchmark by design.
First, the recall curves are sharp at the beginning and flatten out later, and the recall for the top 5 pages is about 69%. This is comparable to what we observe in practice when developing a RAG system. The non-perfect coverage, especially for Task 1, allows us to test whether the RAG solutions admit “I don’t know” when the retrieval results do not contain the necessary information.
Second, compared to the recall from web snippets, full web pages increase the recall by about 20%, emphasizing the importance of extracting and understanding HTML contents. Moreover, the estimated web search recall (50 web pages) is <math alttext="93\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1"><semantics id="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1a"><mrow id="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1.1" xref="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1.1.cmml"><mn id="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1.1.2" mathcolor="#000000" xref="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml">93</mn><mo id="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1.1.1" mathcolor="#000000" xref="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1b"><apply id="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1.1.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1.1.2">93</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1c">93\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S3.SS2.p4.1.1.m1.1d">93 %</annotation></semantics></math> for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.1">Web Questions</span> and <math alttext="74\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1"><semantics id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1a"><mrow id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1.1" xref="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1.1.cmml"><mn id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1.1.2" mathcolor="#000000" xref="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1.1.2.cmml">74</mn><mo id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1.1.1" mathcolor="#000000" xref="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1.1.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1b"><apply id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1.1.cmml" xref="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1.1.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1.1.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1.1.2">74</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1c">74\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.m2.1d">74 %</annotation></semantics></math> for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.SS2.p4.2.2.2">KG Questions</span>, indicating significantly lower recall for KG questions than web questions.
This aligns with our observations that web search recall for torso and tail entities is typically lower, underlining the crucial role of leveraging KGs in Task 2 and 3.</span></p>
</div>
<figure class="ltx_figure" id="S3.F2"><img alt="Refer to caption" class="ltx_graphics ltx_centering ltx_img_landscape" height="330" id="S3.F2.g1" src="x2.png" width="664"/>
<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure">Figure 2: </span>For <math alttext="85\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S3.F2.2.m1.1"><semantics id="S3.F2.2.m1.1b"><mrow id="S3.F2.2.m1.1.1" xref="S3.F2.2.m1.1.1.cmml"><mn id="S3.F2.2.m1.1.1.2" xref="S3.F2.2.m1.1.1.2.cmml">85</mn><mo id="S3.F2.2.m1.1.1.1" xref="S3.F2.2.m1.1.1.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S3.F2.2.m1.1c"><apply id="S3.F2.2.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="S3.F2.2.m1.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="S3.F2.2.m1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S3.F2.2.m1.1.1.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="S3.F2.2.m1.1.1.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S3.F2.2.m1.1.1.2">85</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S3.F2.2.m1.1d">85\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S3.F2.2.m1.1e">85 %</annotation></semantics></math> of CRAG questions, the web search results are estimated to contain the ground truth facts. The curve shows that the retrieval recall grows sharply at the beginning and flattens out later on. </figcaption>
</figure>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.SS2.p5">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.SS2.p5.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S3.SS2.p5.1.1">Mock KGs.</span>
We created mock KGs that contain publicly available KG data used to generate the questions, randomly selected entities of the same type, and also “hard negative” entities with similar names (e.g., <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.SS2.p5.1.2">“phantom”</span> for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S3.SS2.p5.1.3">“phantom of the opera”</span>).</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.SS2.p6">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.SS2.p6.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S3.SS2.p6.1.1">Mock APIs.</span>
We created mock APIs with pre-defined parameters to support structured search in the mock KGs. For example, for queries asking for stock prices, an example mock API is in the form of <code class="ltx_verbatim ltx_font_typewriter" id="S3.SS2.p6.1.2">get_price_history(ticker)</code>.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.SS2.p7">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.SS2.p7.1"><span class="ltx_text" id="S3.SS2.p7.1.1" style="color:#000000;">We collected snapshots of the KG and web search data concurrently while posing real-time and fast-changing questions. This approach ensures that we capture the “snapshot” of the information world at the time of question answering. A RAG solution that performs well on the benchmark should also be capable of reasoning over time and generalizing to evolving questions.</span></p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S3.SS2.p8">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S3.SS2.p8.1">In total, the resulting data contains 220K webpages, a KG of 2.6M entities, and 38 mock APIs. <span class="ltx_text" id="S3.SS2.p8.1.1" style="color:#000000;">See Table <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.T9" title="Table 9 ‣ A.1.6 The mock data and mock APIs ‣ A.1 Dataset ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">9</span></a> in the Appendix for a complete list of the mock APIs.</span></p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_section" id="S4">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">4 </span>Metrics and Evaluation</h2>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S4.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.p1.1">In this section, we present the metrics for evaluating the RAG systems and briefly describe the 2024 Meta KDD Cup challenge in Appendix <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS2.SSS3" title="A.2.3 KDD Cup 2024 Meta CRAG challenge ‣ A.2 Evaluation ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.2.3</span></a>.</p>
</div>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="S4.SS1">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">4.1 </span>Metrics</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S4.SS1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS1.p1.1">We use a scoring method to assess the performance of RAG systems. For each question in the evaluation set, we first label the answer with <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S4.SS1.p1.1.1">perfect, acceptable, missing,</span> or <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S4.SS1.p1.1.2">incorrect</span>, according to the following criteria.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S4.SS1.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS1.p2.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S4.SS1.p2.1.1">Perfect.</span> The response correctly answers the user’s question and contains no hallucinated content.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S4.SS1.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS1.p3.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S4.SS1.p3.1.1">Acceptable.</span> The response provides a useful answer to the user’s question but may contain minor errors that do not harm the usefulness of the answer.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S4.SS1.p4">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS1.p4.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S4.SS1.p4.1.1">Missing.</span> The response is “I don’t know”, “I’m sorry I can’t find …”, a system error such as an empty response, or a request from the system to clarify the original question.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S4.SS1.p5">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS1.p5.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S4.SS1.p5.1.1">Incorrect.</span> The response provides wrong or irrelevant information to answer the user’s question.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S4.SS1.p6">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS1.p6.4">We use a scoring method with score <math alttext="1" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS1.p6.1.m1.1"><semantics id="S4.SS1.p6.1.m1.1a"><mn id="S4.SS1.p6.1.m1.1.1" xref="S4.SS1.p6.1.m1.1.1.cmml">1</mn><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS1.p6.1.m1.1b"><cn id="S4.SS1.p6.1.m1.1.1.cmml" type="integer" xref="S4.SS1.p6.1.m1.1.1">1</cn></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS1.p6.1.m1.1c">1</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS1.p6.1.m1.1d">1</annotation></semantics></math>, <math alttext="0.5" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS1.p6.2.m2.1"><semantics id="S4.SS1.p6.2.m2.1a"><mn id="S4.SS1.p6.2.m2.1.1" xref="S4.SS1.p6.2.m2.1.1.cmml">0.5</mn><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS1.p6.2.m2.1b"><cn id="S4.SS1.p6.2.m2.1.1.cmml" type="float" xref="S4.SS1.p6.2.m2.1.1">0.5</cn></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS1.p6.2.m2.1c">0.5</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS1.p6.2.m2.1d">0.5</annotation></semantics></math>, <math alttext="0" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS1.p6.3.m3.1"><semantics id="S4.SS1.p6.3.m3.1a"><mn id="S4.SS1.p6.3.m3.1.1" xref="S4.SS1.p6.3.m3.1.1.cmml">0</mn><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS1.p6.3.m3.1b"><cn id="S4.SS1.p6.3.m3.1.1.cmml" type="integer" xref="S4.SS1.p6.3.m3.1.1">0</cn></annotation-xml></semantics></math>, and <math alttext="-1" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1"><semantics id="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1a"><mrow id="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1.1" xref="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1.1.cmml"><mo id="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1.1a" xref="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1.1.cmml">−</mo><mn id="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1.1.2" xref="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1.1.2.cmml">1</mn></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1b"><apply id="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1.1"><minus id="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1.1"></minus><cn id="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1.1.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1.1.2">1</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1c">-1</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS1.p6.4.m4.1d">- 1</annotation></semantics></math> for each <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS1.p6.4.1">perfect, acceptable, missing</span>, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS1.p6.4.2">incorrect</span> answer, respectively, where we penalize hallucinated answers and prefer <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS1.p6.4.3">missing</span> answers to <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS1.p6.4.4">incorrect</span> ones. <span class="ltx_text" id="S4.SS1.p6.4.5" style="color:#000000;">We then define <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S4.SS1.p6.4.5.1">truthfulness</span> as the average score from all examples in the evaluation set for a given RAG system.</span></p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="S4.SS2">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">4.2 </span>Evaluation</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S4.SS2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS2.p1.1">Similar to previous work <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib37" title="">37</a>]</cite>, we employ both human evaluation <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.1">(human-eval)</span> and model-based automatic evaluation <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.2">(auto-eval)</span>. In the former, we use manual grading to judge <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.3">perfect, acceptable, missing</span>, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.4">incorrect</span> for each answer. In the latter, we merge <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.5">perfect</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.6">acceptable</span>, call it <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.7">accurate</span>, and use a three-way scoring system with <math alttext="1,-1,0" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3"><semantics id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3a"><mrow id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.2.cmml"><mn id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1.1" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml">1</mn><mo id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.2" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.2.cmml">,</mo><mrow id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.1" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.1.cmml"><mo id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.1a" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.1.cmml">−</mo><mn id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.1.2" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.1.2.cmml">1</mn></mrow><mo id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.3" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.2.cmml">,</mo><mn id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.2.2" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.2.2.cmml">0</mn></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3b"><list id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.2.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1"><cn id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml" type="integer" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1.1">1</cn><apply id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.1"><minus id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.1"></minus><cn id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.1.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3.3.1.1.2">1</cn></apply><cn id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.2.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.2.2">0</cn></list></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3c">1,-1,0</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.3d">1 , - 1 , 0</annotation></semantics></math> for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.8">accurate</span>, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.9">incorrect</span>, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.10">missing</span> answers.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S4.SS2.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS2.p2.2">We design a two-step method for automatic evaluation: if the answer matches the ground truth exactly, it is considered <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.1">accurate</span>; otherwise, we use LLMs to determine whether the response is <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.2">accurate, incorrect</span>, or <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.3">missing</span>. To avoid the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.4">self-preference</span> problem <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib25" title="">25</a>]</cite>, we use two LLM evaluators: ChatGPT (<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.5">gpt-3.5-turbo-0125</span>) <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib24" title="">24</a>]</cite> and Llama 3 (<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.6">llama-3-70B-instruct</span>) <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib2" title="">2</a>]</cite> and report the average <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.7">accurate, hallucination, missing</span> rates, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.8" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> scores from the two models for each RAG system. Our offline experiment shows that this two-step method yields an average F1 score of <math alttext="94.7\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1"><semantics id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1a"><mrow id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.cmml"><mn id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.2" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml">94.7</mn><mo id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.1" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1b"><apply id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml" type="float" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.2">94.7</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1c">94.7\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1d">94.7 %</annotation></semantics></math> for ChatGPT and <math alttext="98.9\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1"><semantics id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1a"><mrow id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1" xref="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1.cmml"><mn id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1.2" xref="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1.2.cmml">98.9</mn><mo id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1.1" xref="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1b"><apply id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1.2.cmml" type="float" xref="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1.2">98.9</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1c">98.9\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1d">98.9 %</annotation></semantics></math> for Llama 3 compared to human-eval. See Appendix <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS2.SSS2" title="A.2.2 Automatic evaluation ‣ A.2 Evaluation ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.2.2</span></a> for more details.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S4.SS2.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS2.p3.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S4.SS2.p3.1.1">Test data split.</span>
We split the data randomly into <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p3.1.2">validation</span> (30%), <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p3.1.3">public test</span> (30%), and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS2.p3.1.4">private</span> (40%), and released the validation and public test sets (Appendix <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS2.SSS3" title="A.2.3 KDD Cup 2024 Meta CRAG challenge ‣ A.2 Evaluation ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.2.3</span></a>). Participants of the KDD Cup challenge can use the validation and public test sets to develop and test their models, and the submitted solutions were evaluated on the private test set. Future offline users of CRAG can use the validation set for development, fine-tuning, and validation, and the public test set for testing and result reporting.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_section" id="S5">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">5 </span>Benchmarking</h2>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S5.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S5.p1.1">In this section, we present the performance of LLMs and RAG systems on CRAG, demonstrating that CRAG has a reasonable level of difficulty and can help draw insights and show directions in developing RAG techniques.</p>
</div>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="S5.SS1">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">5.1 </span>Straightforward RAG solutions</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S5.SS1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S5.SS1.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.1">Experiment setup:</span> We started with running LLM-only solutions on the CRAG public test set with <math alttext="1,335" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2"><semantics id="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2a"><mrow id="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2.3.2" xref="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2.3.1.cmml"><mn id="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.1.1" xref="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml">1</mn><mo id="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2.3.2.1" xref="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2.3.1.cmml">,</mo><mn id="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2.2" xref="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2.2.cmml">335</mn></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2b"><list id="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2.3.1.cmml" xref="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2.3.2"><cn id="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml" type="integer" xref="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.1.1">1</cn><cn id="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2.2">335</cn></list></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2c">1,335</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.m1.2d">1 , 335</annotation></semantics></math> questions, using simple prompts that encourage brief answers and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.2">“I don’t know”</span> answers when the confidence is low (Appendix <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS3.SSS1" title="A.3.1 Prompts used in straightforward RAG solutions ‣ A.3 Evaluating straightforward RAG solutions ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.3.1</span></a>). We employed Llama 2 Chat (<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.3">llama-2-7b-chat</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.4">llama-2-70b-chat</span>) <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib34" title="">34</a>]</cite>, Llama 3 Instruct (<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.5">llama-3-8B-instruct</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.6">llama-3-70B-instruct</span>) <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib2" title="">2</a>]</cite>, <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.7" style="color:#000000;">Mixtral (<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.7.1">Mixtral-8x7B-Instruct-v0.1</span>) <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib15" title="">15</a>]</cite>, Falcon (<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.7.2">40B</span>) <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib3" title="">3</a>]</cite>, FLAN-T5 (<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.7.3">FLAN-T5-XXL</span>) <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib9" title="">9</a>]</cite>, and GPT-4 Turbo (<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.7.4">gpt-4-turbo-2024-04-09</span>) <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib1" title="">1</a>]</cite></span>. The web-only RAG solutions we evaluated (Task 1) used a fixed-length web context window (<span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.8" style="color:#000000;">1K tokens for Falcon and FLAN-T5</span>, 2K for Llama 2 Chat, and 4K for Llama 3 Instruct and GPT-4 Turbo); we concatenated webpage snippets using the original order from the data as the reference text, until filling up the window (similar to <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib36" title="">36</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib17" title="">17</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib23" title="">23</a>]</cite>). Our KG-based solutions (Tasks 2, 3) additionally used a fixed-length KG context window (<span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.9" style="color:#000000;">0.5K tokens for Falcon and FLAN-T5</span>, 1K for Llama 2 Chat, and 2K for Llama 3 Instruct and GPT-4 Turbo) to include the results from the mock APIs; we extracted the relevant query entities using <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="S5.SS1.p1.1.10">llama-3-8B-instruct</span> with in-context learning (similar to <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib28" title="">28</a>]</cite>) detailed in Appendix <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS3.SSS1" title="A.3.1 Prompts used in straightforward RAG solutions ‣ A.3 Evaluating straightforward RAG solutions ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.3.1</span></a> and concatenated the results returned from all applicable mock APIs (based on the extracted entities), until filling up the window. We provide an extensive comparison of all LLMs in Appendix <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS3.SSS2" title="A.3.2 Performance of straightforward RAG solutions ‣ A.3 Evaluating straightforward RAG solutions ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.3.2</span></a> and focus on the best-performing LLMs (i.e., Llama 3 70B Instruct and GPT-4 Turbo) in this section.</p>
</div>
<figure class="ltx_table" id="S5.T5">
<figcaption class="ltx_caption"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_table">Table 5: </span>Performance of straightforward RAG solutions. All numbers are in percentage. <figure class="ltx_figure" id="S5.F3"><img alt="Refer to caption" class="ltx_graphics ltx_centering ltx_img_landscape" height="417" id="S5.F3.g1" src="x3.png" width="830"/>
<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure">Figure 3: </span>LLM-only and Task 3 solution auto-eval truthfulness (in percentage) across domain, dynamism, popularity, and question type.</figcaption>
</figure>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S5.SS1.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S5.SS1.p2.1">Table <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S5.T5" title="Table 5 ‣ 5.1 Straightforward RAG solutions ‣ 5 Benchmarking ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">5</span></a> shows the average evaluation results from the two auto-evaluators (ChatGPT and Llama 3) and illustrates that the CRAG benchmark is <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p2.1.1">non-trivial</span>. First, the best LLM-only solutions (GPT-4 Turbo) obtained an accuracy of only 34%, with <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p2.1.2" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> of 20%, showing a big room for improvement. Second, straightforward RAG solutions obtained up to 44% accuracy, showing that extra information <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p2.1.3">does</span> help answer more questions reliably. Interestingly, none of the RAG solutions obtain <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p2.1.4" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> higher than 20%; this is because all RAG solutions introduce more hallucinations generated from irrelevant retrieval results, showing a big challenge in RAG—<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p2.1.5">How to judiciously use retrieval results without being distracted by retrieval noises?</span> Third, we found that Task 2 <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p2.1.6" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness scores</span> are higher than Task 1, showing that the KG knowledge helps improve accuracy, with a similar or even lower hallucination rate, because the KG knowledge is typically brief but precise. Unfortunately, the improvement is mediocre, showing a second challenge in RAG—<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p2.1.7">How to best leverage the power of KG data?</span> Finally, the <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p2.1.8" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> for Task 3 are also higher than Task 2, because of better search ranking (recall that Task 1 and 2 provide five pages randomly selected from the top-10 search results) and better search recall. <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p2.1.9" style="color:#000000;">In particular, we found that the ground truths of over 30% of questions are available in the web retrieval results but are not included in the prompt due to the context window limitation.</span> This shows <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p2.1.10">the importance of search ranking</span> in RAG.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S5.SS1.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S5.SS1.p3.1">Figure <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S5.F3" title="Figure 3 ‣ 5.1 Straightforward RAG solutions ‣ 5 Benchmarking ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">3</span></a> shows the auto-eval results across the domain, dynamism, popularity, and question type dimension. The results reveal a lot of interesting observations and show that the CRAG benchmark allows more <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.1">insightful</span> conclusions. First, it shows <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.2">which slices of the benchmark are harder</span>. For example, we found much lower RAG <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.3" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> on the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.4">Finance</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.5">Sports</span> domains, for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.6">real-time</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.7">fast-changing</span> facts, for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.8">tail</span> entities, and for complex questions requiring <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.9">set answers, post-processing,</span> and with <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.10">false premises</span>. Second, it shows <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.11">where it is harder to leverage retrieval results</span>. Take the popularity slices as an example, we observed that GPT-4 Turbo’s <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.12" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> dropped from head (21%) to torso (11%) to tail (8%), consistent with past observations <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib29" title="">29</a>]</cite>; however, the straightforward RAG solution based on GPT-4 Turbo improved QA quality regarding torso (+7%) and tail entities (+6%) but lowered the quality regarding head (-4%).
Finally, although our goal is <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.13">not</span> to compare different LLMs, the different dimensions allow us to understand the strengths and weaknesses of each method. For example, although the RAG system based on Llama 3 70B Instruct has a lower overall <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.14" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness score</span> than the one based on GPT-4 Turbo, it has a similar or slightly higher <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.15" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> in answering <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.16">simple</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.17">comparison</span> questions, whereas much lower <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.18" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> in answering <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.19">set</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS1.p3.1.20">post-processing</span> questions, suggesting investigations on the reasoning capabilities.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="S5.SS2">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">5.2 </span>State-of-the-art industry solutions</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S5.SS2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S5.SS2.p1.1">Next, we evaluated industry state-of-the-art (SOTA) RAG solutions on CRAG public test set. We selected five RAG systems built upon SOTA LLMs and search engines, queried them with CRAG questions, collected the responses, and applied manual grading (details in Appendix <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS4" title="A.4 Evaluating state-of-the-art industry solutions ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.4</span></a>).</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S5.SS2.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S5.SS2.p2.1">In addition, we applied traffic weights to the questions to understand the solutions in real-world use cases. <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS2.p2.1.1" style="color:#000000;">The traffic weights reflect the frequency of each question type, as defined in Table <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S3.T2" title="Table 2 ‣ 3 Dataset Description ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">2</span></a>, in real QA traffic. We gave the same weights to all domains and reported the macro average across domains. This is because we have observed quite different domain-level distributions in different use cases, but have been observing similar distributions at the query-type level.</span></p>
</div>
<figure class="ltx_table" id="S5.T6">
<figcaption class="ltx_caption"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_table">Table 6: </span>Benchmarking CRAG questions with industry SOTA RAG systems.
