The best system achieves <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.T6.7.3" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> of 51% and provides perfect answers for up to 63% of questions.</figcaption>

<figure class="ltx_figure" id="S5.F4"><img alt="Refer to caption" class="ltx_graphics ltx_centering ltx_img_landscape" height="414" id="S5.F4.g1" src="x4.png" width="830"/>
<figcaption class="ltx_caption ltx_centering"><span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_figure">Figure 4: </span>SOTA systems human-eval <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.F4.2.1" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness scores</span> (in percentage) across different dimensions.
</figcaption>
</figure>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S5.SS2.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S5.SS2.p3.3">Table <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S5.T6" title="Table 6 ‣ 5.2 State-of-the-art industry solutions ‣ 5 Benchmarking ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">6</span></a> and Figure <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S5.F4" title="Figure 4 ‣ 5.2 State-of-the-art industry solutions ‣ 5 Benchmarking ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">4</span></a> show the overall performance of the SOTA systems and their performance across different dimensions. The evaluation results confirm our belief that the CRAG benchmark <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.3">reveals interesting insights and shows room for improvement for existing RAG solutions.</span>
First, the results from SOTA solutions achieve much better <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.4" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> (highest <math alttext="51\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1"><semantics id="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1a"><mrow id="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1.1" xref="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1.1.cmml"><mn id="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1.1.2" xref="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml">51</mn><mo id="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1.1.1" xref="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1b"><apply id="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1.1.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1.1.2">51</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1c">51\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S5.SS2.p3.1.m1.1d">51 %</annotation></semantics></math>) compared to the straightforward solutions. However, the hallucination rate ranges from <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.5" style="color:#000000;">16%</span> to 25%, so the answers are still <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.6">not</span> trustworthy. Note that the <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.7" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness scores</span> between the SOTA solutions and the straightforward solutions are not completely comparable, as they have different accesses to retrieval contents (Appendix <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS3" title="A.3 Evaluating straightforward RAG solutions ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.3</span></a> and <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS4.SSS1" title="A.4.1 Quality ‣ A.4 Evaluating state-of-the-art industry solutions ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.4.1</span></a>), and the former used auto-eval, while the latter used human-eval; however, the trend is valid.
<span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.2" style="color:#000000;">Second, we observed very different latency, ranging from <math alttext="3.4" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S5.SS2.p3.2.1.m1.1"><semantics id="S5.SS2.p3.2.1.m1.1a"><mn id="S5.SS2.p3.2.1.m1.1.1" mathcolor="#000000" xref="S5.SS2.p3.2.1.m1.1.1.cmml">3.4</mn><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S5.SS2.p3.2.1.m1.1b"><cn id="S5.SS2.p3.2.1.m1.1.1.cmml" type="float" xref="S5.SS2.p3.2.1.m1.1.1">3.4</cn></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S5.SS2.p3.2.1.m1.1c">3.4</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S5.SS2.p3.2.1.m1.1d">3.4</annotation></semantics></math>s to <math alttext="11.6" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.2.m2.1"><semantics id="S5.SS2.p3.3.2.m2.1a"><mn id="S5.SS2.p3.3.2.m2.1.1" mathcolor="#000000" xref="S5.SS2.p3.3.2.m2.1.1.cmml">11.6</mn><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.2.m2.1b"><cn id="S5.SS2.p3.3.2.m2.1.1.cmml" type="float" xref="S5.SS2.p3.3.2.m2.1.1">11.6</cn></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.2.m2.1c">11.6</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.2.m2.1d">11.6</annotation></semantics></math>s, reflecting the different design options in trading off latency and quality; for example, Copilot Pro has the highest truthfulness, but meanwhile highest latency, whereas Meta SG <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib10" title="">10</a>]</cite> has mid-tier truthfulness but lowest latency. (See Appendix <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.SS4.SSS2" title="A.4.2 Latency ‣ A.4 Evaluating state-of-the-art industry solutions ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">A.4.2</span></a> for additional results and how we measured latency.)
Third,</span> most difficult slices we see in the straightforward solutions remain to be difficult for SOTA solutions: <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.8">real-time</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.9">fast-changing</span> queries, and questions regarding <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.10">torso</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.11">tail</span> entities, showing the improvement needed for handling retrieval noises when the system relies on retrieval results to answer the question; as another example, we see lower <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.12" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> for queries requiring <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.13">aggregation, multi-hop reasoning</span> or <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.14">post-processing</span>, showing the improvement space for reasoning in question answering.
Last, <span class="ltx_text" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.15" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> on <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.16">set</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.17">false premise</span> questions improved significantly in the SOTA solutions compared to the straightforward solutions, showing advancement in RAG systems in providing accurate and complete set answers and detecting <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S5.SS2.p3.3.18">false premises</span>.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_section" id="S6">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_section">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_section">6 </span>Conclusion</h2>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="S6.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S6.p1.1">This paper proposes CRAG, a rich and comprehensive benchmark designed to advance research in retrieval-augmented generation (RAG). With detailed empirical studies, CRAG reviewed gaps in existing RAG solutions and provided valuable insights for future improvement.
We plan to continue improving and expanding the benchmark for multi-lingual questions, multi-modal questions, multi-turn conversations, etc., to ensure CRAG stays at the forefront to push RAG research, adapts to emerging challenges, and evolves for new research needs.</p>
</div>
</section>

<section class="ltx_appendix ltx_pruned_first" id="A1">
<h2 class="ltx_title ltx_title_appendix">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_appendix">Appendix A </span>Appendix</h2>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A1.SS1">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">A.1 </span>Dataset</h3>
<section class="ltx_subsubsection" id="A1.SS1.SSS1">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">A.1.1 </span>Constructing QA pairs from KGs</h4>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p1.1">We first collected a set of entities based on publicly available data. Then we created question-answer pairs in three steps for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p1.1.1">Simple static and dynamic questions</span>.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.1">Step 1.</span> For each domain, we first selected an entity type and a meaningful relation <math alttext="(e,r)" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2"><semantics id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2a"><mrow id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.3.2" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.3.1.cmml"><mo id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.3.2.1" stretchy="false" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.3.1.cmml">(</mo><mi id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.1.1" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.1.1.cmml">e</mi><mo id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.3.2.2" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.3.1.cmml">,</mo><mi id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.2" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.2.cmml">r</mi><mo id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.3.2.3" stretchy="false" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.3.1.cmml">)</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2b"><interval closure="open" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.3.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.3.2"><ci id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.1.1">𝑒</ci><ci id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.2.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2.2">𝑟</ci></interval></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2c">(e,r)</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.m1.2d">( italic_e , italic_r )</annotation></semantics></math> and created a question template. For example, for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.2">(music artist, first album)</span>, we create a template “<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p2.1.3">what is the first album of [music artist]?</span>”.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p3.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p3.1.1">Step 2.</span> We then sampled entities from the KGs to fill in the templates and generate the full question. We adopted the method described in <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib29" title="">29</a>]</cite> and sampled entities of top, middle, and bottom popularity. We defined popularity based on heuristics for each entity type and created an equal number of questions for each bucket.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p4">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p4.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p4.1.1">Step 3.</span>
Last, we took the associated attribute values as the answer to the question to create question-answer pairs.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p5">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p5.1">We created the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p5.1.1">Comparison, Aggregation, Set, Post-processing</span>, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p5.1.2">False-premise questions</span> in a similar way but 1) made sure the template allows for crisp and deterministic answers and 2) sampled the subject entities that fit the question. We used heuristics to select entity types for these question categories.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8">Finally, we created multi-hop questions in three steps, similar to those described in <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib31" title="">31</a>]</cite>. We first sampled an entity <math alttext="e_{1}" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1"><semantics id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1a"><msub id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1.1" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1.1.cmml"><mi id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1.1.2" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml">e</mi><mn id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1.1.3" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1.1.3.cmml">1</mn></msub><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1b"><apply id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1.1.2">𝑒</ci><cn id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1.1.3.cmml" type="integer" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1.1.3">1</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1c">e_{1}</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.1.m1.1d">italic_e start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT</annotation></semantics></math> from the KG and selected two relation triplets following a two-hop path: <math alttext="(e_{1},r_{1},e_{2})" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.2.m2.3"><semantics encoding="MathML-Content" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.3b"><vector id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.3.3.4.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.3.3.3"><apply id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.1.1.1.1"><csymbol cd="ambiguous" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.1.1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.1.1.1.1">subscript</csymbol><ci id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.1.1.1.1.2.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.1.1.1.1.2">𝑒</ci><cn id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.1.1.1.1.3.cmml" type="integer" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.1.1.1.1.3">1</cn></apply><apply id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.2.2.2.2.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.2.2.2.2"><csymbol cd="ambiguous" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.2.2.2.2.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.2.2.2.2">subscript</csymbol><ci id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.2.2.2.2.2.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.3.3.3.3"><csymbol cd="ambiguous" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.3.3.3.3.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.3.3.3.3">subscript</csymbol><ci id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.3.3.3.3.2.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.3.3.3.3.2">𝑒</ci><cn id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.3.3.3.3.3.cmml" type="integer" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.3.3.3.3.3">3</cn></apply></vector></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.3c">(e_{1},r_{2},e_{3})</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.3.m3.3d">( italic_e start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , italic_r start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 2 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , italic_e start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 3 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT )</annotation></semantics></math>. We then created a question template describing the path. For example, for path <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.5.2">(company<sub class="ltx_sub" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.5.2.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_upright" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.5.2.1.1">1</span></sub>, is_parent, company<sub class="ltx_sub" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.5.2.2"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_upright" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.5.2.2.1">2</span></sub>)</span> followed by <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.6.3">(company<sub class="ltx_sub" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.6.3.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_upright" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.6.3.1.1">1</span></sub>, ceo, person)</span>, we created the template <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.7.4">"who is the CEO of the parent company of [company<sub class="ltx_sub" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.7.4.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_upright" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.7.4.1.1">2</span></sub>]?"</span>. The answer to the new question will be <math alttext="e_{3}" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1"><semantics id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1a"><msub id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1.cmml"><mi id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1.2" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1.2.cmml">e</mi><mn id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1.3" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1.3.cmml">3</mn></msub><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1b"><apply id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1"><csymbol cd="ambiguous" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1">subscript</csymbol><ci id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1.2.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1.2">𝑒</ci><cn id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1.3.cmml" type="integer" xref="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1.1.3">3</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1c">e_{3}</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="A1.SS1.SSS1.p6.8.m4.1d">italic_e start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 3 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT</annotation></semantics></math> in the second triplet.</p>
</div>
</section>

<section class="ltx_subsubsection" id="A1.SS1.SSS3">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">A.1.3 </span>Constructing QA pairs from web contents</h4>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p1.1.1">Step 1.</span> Ask annotators to write down a list of questions that could possibly be answered by web search based on a general guideline (e.g., “<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p1.1.2">what is the most popular action movie in 2023?</span>”).</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p2.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p2.1.1">Step 2.</span> Generate the web search results to answer the question.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p3.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p3.1.1">Step 3.</span> Finally, annotators reviewed the web search results to determine the ground truth answers to the questions:
1) If the search results successfully provided the necessary information, annotators recorded the ground truth answer text and the URL associated with it based on the retrieved content. Note that the answer is determined by the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p3.1.2">query_time</span> at which the web search happened, especially for the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p3.1.3">Fast-changing</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p3.1.4">Real-time</span> questions.
2) Otherwise, annotators conducted further web searches to document the correct answers.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p4">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p4.1">Besides the QA pairs, the annotators will also provide labels for the domain, dynamism, question types, and an <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p4.1.1">answer URL</span> (a URL that contains the answer to the question) for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS3.p4.1.2">Web Questions</span>.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsubsection" id="A1.SS1.SSS4">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">A.1.4 </span>Validation for the QA pairs</h4>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p1.1">We conducted two phases of dataset validation with our in-house Linguist team.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.1">Phase 1. Question and meta-label validation.</span> After the initial round of QA pair generation, an audit session was conducted, where expert annotators reviewed the question template, questions, and meta-labels (domain, question type, etc), applying edits as necessary with 2x human review (agreement rate <math alttext="90\%+" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1"><semantics id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1a"><mrow id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.cmml"><mrow id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.2" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml"><mn id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.2" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.2.cmml">90</mn><mo id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.1" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><mo id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.3" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.3.cmml">+</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1b"><apply id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1">limit-from</csymbol><apply id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.2"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.2">90</cn></apply><plus id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.3.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1.1.3"></plus></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1c">90\%+</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p2.1.m1.1d">90 % +</annotation></semantics></math>). All problematic questions (e.g., a wrong false-premise question) were revised, and all conflicting labels were resolved by a third more experienced auditor.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.1">Phase 2. Answer validation.</span> To ensure the answers in the benchmark are correct, we further conducted an auditing process for all the answers.
For the web questions, an annotation team reviewed each question and conducted an extensive search to make sure the answer is factually correct and includes comprehensive information (such as for set questions) with 2x human review (agreement rate <math alttext="90\%+" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1"><semantics id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1a"><mrow id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.cmml"><mrow id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.2" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml"><mn id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.2.2" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.2.2.cmml">90</mn><mo id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.2.1" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.2.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><mo id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.3" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.3.cmml">+</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1b"><apply id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1">limit-from</csymbol><apply id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.2"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.2.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.2.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.2.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.2.2">90</cn></apply><plus id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.3.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1.1.3"></plus></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1c">90\%+</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.1.m1.1d">90 % +</annotation></semantics></math>). A third more experienced auditor then reviewed all conflicting answers and provided a resolution.
For the KG questions, a team of five engineers carefully checked the questions and queried the mock APIs manually to validate the answers. This step resulted in a <math alttext="5\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1"><semantics id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1a"><mrow id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1.1" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1.1.cmml"><mn id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1.1.2" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1.1.2.cmml">5</mn><mo id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1.1.1" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1.1.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1b"><apply id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1.1.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1.1.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1.1.2">5</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1c">5\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p3.2.m2.1d">5 %</annotation></semantics></math> answer correction.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1">In both phases, we paid special attention to examples where the straightforward solutions output different answers from the ground truth answers and asked the auditing team to double-check those examples. This step yielded an additional <math alttext="2\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1"><semantics id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1a"><mrow id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1.1" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1.1.cmml"><mn id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1.1.2" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml">2</mn><mo id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1.1.1" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1b"><apply id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1.1.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1.1.2">2</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1c">2\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="A1.SS1.SSS4.p4.1.m1.1d">2 %</annotation></semantics></math> answer updates.</p>
</div>
</section>

<section class="ltx_subsubsection" id="A1.SS1.SSS6">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">A.1.6 </span>The mock data and mock APIs</h4>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS6.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS6.p1.1">CRAG provides mock APIs to simulate retrieval from web, KG, and real-time APIs in the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS6.p1.1.1">real</span> retrieval environment, allowing <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS1.SSS6.p1.1.2">accessible</span> facilitating data and fair comparison.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS1.SSS6.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS1.SSS6.p2.1">CRAG provides both structured (through mock KGs) and unstructured (web search results) information to test the effectiveness of RAG systems in leveraging a diverse range of available information. First, for each question in the benchmark, CRAG provides up to 50 web search results from a real-world search engine—the Brave Search API <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib5" title="">5</a>]</cite>. Different from existing benchmarks that use snippets or selected text chunks <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite">[<a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib4" title="">4</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#bib.bib6" title="">6</a>]</cite>, CRAG provides full HTML pages, containing more information and potentially more noises as in a realistic setting. Second, CRAG provides mock KG search APIs to test structured search for RAG. The mock KGs, though much smaller in size, contain both information necessary to answer a subset of questions in the benchmark and noises that have similar entity or attribute names, again simulating real settings. Our mock KGs contain about 2.6M entities and have a signal-to-noise ratio of less than 1/30.</p>
</div>
<figure class="ltx_table" id="A1.T9">

<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A1.SS2">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">A.2 </span>Evaluation</h3>
<section class="ltx_subsubsection" id="A1.SS2.SSS1">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">A.2.1 </span>Human evaluation</h4>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p1.9">We run human evaluation to score each answer with respect to the metrics defined in Section <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S4.SS1" title="4.1 Metrics ‣ 4 Metrics and Evaluation ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">4.1</span></a>. We score each <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p1.9.2">perfect, acceptable, missing</span>, or <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p1.9.3">incorrect</span> answer with a score <math alttext="s_{p}" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p1.1.m1.1"><semantics id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p1.1.m1.1a"><msub id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p1.1.m1.1.1" We then compute the average <span class="ltx_text" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p1.9.4" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> for all examples in the evaluation set as the <span class="ltx_text" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p1.9.5" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> score for the RAG solution.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p2.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p2.1.1" style="color:#000000;">Human-eval instructions.<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_medium" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p2.1.1.1"> The human-eval instructions are as follows.
<br class="ltx_break"/>Given a query, a query day and time at which the query was made, the chatbot’s response, grade the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p2.1.1.1.1">accuracy</span> for the response according to the criteria below:
<br class="ltx_break"/>Using an external search engine, please evaluate the factual accuracy of the response based on the grading rubric below. An accurate answer should be factually correct and provide useful information to answer the user’s question.</span></span></p>
<ul class="ltx_itemize" id="A1.I1">
<li class="ltx_item" id="A1.I1.i1" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A1.I1.i1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.I1.i1.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text" id="A1.I1.i1.p1.1.1" style="color:#000000;">Accuracy = 0 (Missing). It covers the following situations.
There is no response.
There is a failure to provide a response to the request (e.g. “I’m sorry ……, I can’t do …”) due to inability.
E.g.,
Query: “Latest news about the Nobel prize today.”
Response: “I can’t find specific information regarding the Nobel prize …”
The response fails to answer and asks follow-up questions.</span></p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A1.I1.i2" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A1.I1.i2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.I1.i2.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text" id="A1.I1.i2.p1.1.1" style="color:#000000;">Accuracy = 1 (Incorrect). It covers the following situations.
The answer is unintelligible.
The answer is poorly formed.
The answer contains a major hallucination (e.g. wrong date, wrong numbers, or other significant factual errors).
The answer is irrelevant to the user’s request.
Answers in a category, location, or time window that is significantly different from the user’s request, if any.
There is a significant structural/formatting error.
The response is otherwise a total structural/functional failure and does not contain sufficient well-formed content that can be used to determine accuracy</span></p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A1.I1.i3" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para" id="A1.I1.i3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.I1.i3.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text" id="A1.I1.i3.p1.1.1" style="color:#000000;">Accuracy = 2 (Acceptable). It covers the following situations.
The answer is acceptably correct and relevant to the user’s request, but may miss some information, i.e. accurate but not complete, or mostly accurate with minor issues.
The answer may contain some minor hallucination that doesn’t significantly alter the overall meaning. “Minor hallucination” means the answer addressed the user’s question but might be off on some additional details. The rule of thumb is to see if the answer serves the purpose of the user’s question, and whether the hallucination could mislead the users on what they were asking.</span></p>
</div>
</li>
<li class="ltx_item" id="A1.I1.i4" style="list-style-type:none;">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_item">•</span>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.I1.i4.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.I1.i4.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text" id="A1.I1.i4.p1.1.1" style="color:#000000;">Accuracy = 3 (Accurate).
The answer is factually correct, contains all the relevant information requested, responds appropriately to the query, and does not contain any hallucination.</span></p>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1"><span class="ltx_text" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1" style="color:#000000;">We requested two human graders to grade each question (agreement rate <math alttext="94\%" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1"><semantics id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1a"><mrow id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1.1" xref="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1.1.cmml"><mn id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1.1.2" mathcolor="#000000" xref="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml">94</mn><mo id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1.1.1" mathcolor="#000000" xref="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml">%</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1b"><apply id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1.1"><csymbol cd="latexml" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1.1.1">percent</csymbol><cn id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1.1.2">94</cn></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1c">94\%</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="A1.SS2.SSS1.p3.1.1.m1.1d">94 %</annotation></semantics></math>), and when there is a conflict, a third more experienced grader will resolve it.</span></p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsubsection" id="A1.SS2.SSS2">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">A.2.2 </span>Automatic evaluation</h4>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.1">In auto-eval, we merge <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.1.2">perfect</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.1.3">acceptable</span> as <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.1.4">accurate</span> and consider only three scores: 1 for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.1.5">accurate</span>, 0 for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.1.6">missing</span>, and -1 for <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.1.7">incorrect</span>. The <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.1.1" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness<sub class="ltx_sub" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.1.1.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_medium ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.1.1.1.1">a</span></sub></span> is calculated by the average <span class="ltx_text" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.1.8" style="color:#000000;">truthfulness</span> for all the examples in the evaluation set, and is effectively</p>
<table class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_table" id="A1.Ex1">
<tbody><tr class="ltx_equation ltx_eqn_row ltx_align_baseline">
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padleft"></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_align_center"><math alttext="\text{accuracy}-\text{hallucination}," class="ltx_Math" display="block" id="A1.Ex1.m1.1"><semantics id="A1.Ex1.m1.1a"><mrow id="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1" xref="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.cmml"><mrow id="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1" xref="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.cmml"><mtext id="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.2" xref="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.2a.cmml">accuracy</mtext><mo id="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.1" xref="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.1.cmml">−</mo><mtext id="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.3" xref="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.3a.cmml">hallucination</mtext></mrow><mo id="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.2" xref="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.cmml">,</mo></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="A1.Ex1.m1.1b"><apply id="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1"><minus id="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.1"></minus><ci id="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.2a.cmml" xref="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.2"><mtext id="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.2.cmml" xref="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.2">accuracy</mtext></ci><ci id="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.3a.cmml" xref="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.3"><mtext id="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.3.cmml" xref="A1.Ex1.m1.1.1.1.1.3">hallucination</mtext></ci></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="A1.Ex1.m1.1c">\text{accuracy}-\text{hallucination},</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="A1.Ex1.m1.1d">accuracy - hallucination ,</annotation></semantics></math></td>
<td class="ltx_eqn_cell ltx_eqn_center_padright"></td>
</tr></tbody>
</table>
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.2">where <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.2.1">accuracy</span>, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.2.2">hallucination</span>, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.2.3">missing</span> are the percentage of <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.2.4">accurate</span>, <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.2.5">incorrect</span>, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.2.6">missing</span> answers in the test set. These score choices penalize <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.2.7">incorrect</span> answers, award <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.2.8">correct</span>, and assign a value of 0 to <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p1.2.9">missing</span> answers.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p2.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p2.1.1">Auto-evaluators.</span> We computed the accuracy and F1 for the two auto-evaluators for the <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p2.1.2">accurate, incorrect</span>, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p2.1.3">missing</span> examples in the public test set, respectively. Here, we considered human-eval labels as the ground truth. Table <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#A1.T10" title="Table 10 ‣ A.2.2 Automatic evaluation ‣ A.2 Evaluation ‣ Appendix A Appendix ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">10</span></a> shows both models attain reasonable accuracy and F1 scores as an evaluator compared to human evaluation.</p>
</div>

<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p3.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p3.1.1" style="color:#000000;">Auto-eval prompt.<span class="ltx_text ltx_font_medium" id="A1.SS2.SSS2.p3.1.1.1"> The prompt we used in the auto-eval is similar to the following. We did not release the exact prompt used in the challenge to avoid prompt attack.
<br class="ltx_break"/>PROMPT = """# Task:
You are given a Question, a model Prediction, and a list of Ground Truth answers, judge whether the model Prediction matches any answer from the list of Ground Truth answers. Follow the instructions step by step to make a judgement. 
<br class="ltx_break"/>1. If the model prediction matches any provided answers from the Ground Truth Answer list, "Accuracy" should be "True"; otherwise, "Accuracy" should be "False".
<br class="ltx_break"/>2. If the model prediction says that it couldn’t answer the question or it doesn’t have enough information, "Accuracy" should always be "False".
<br class="ltx_break"/>3. If the Ground Truth is "invalid question", "Accuracy" is "True" only if the model prediction is exactly "invalid question".
<br class="ltx_break"/># Output: 
<br class="ltx_break"/>Respond with only a single JSON string with an "Accuracy" field which is "True" or "False".
<br class="ltx_break"/># Examples:
<br class="ltx_break"/>Question: how many seconds is 3 minutes 15 seconds?
<br class="ltx_break"/>Ground truth: ["195 seconds"]
<br class="ltx_break"/>Prediction: 3 minutes 15 seconds is 195 seconds.
<br class="ltx_break"/>Accuracy: True 
<br class="ltx_break"/>Question: Who authored The Taming of the Shrew (published in 2002)?
<br class="ltx_break"/>Ground truth: ["William Shakespeare", "Roma Gill"]
<br class="ltx_break"/>Prediction: The author to The Taming of the Shrew is Roma Shakespeare.
<br class="ltx_break"/>Accuracy: False 
<br class="ltx_break"/>Question: Who played Sheldon in Big Bang Theory?
<br class="ltx_break"/>Ground truth: ["Jim Parsons", "Iain Armitage"]
<br class="ltx_break"/>Prediction: I am sorry I don’t know.
<br class="ltx_break"/>Accuracy: False
<br class="ltx_break"/>"""
</span></span></p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsubsection" id="A1.SS2.SSS3">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">A.2.3 </span>KDD Cup 2024 Meta CRAG challenge</h4>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS2.SSS3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS2.SSS3.p1.1">The KDD Cup 2024 Meta CRAG challenge has two stages. Stage 1 is designed for the participants to develop their RAG solutions by submitting their systems against the leaderboard, whereas Stage 2 determines the final winners.
We split our benchmark data into three sets with similar distributions: <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS3.p1.1.1">validation, public test</span>, and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS2.SSS3.p1.1.2">private test</span> at 30%, 30%, and 40%, respectively. We shared the validation and public test sets, in total, 2,706 examples in Stage 1, and held out the private test set to select the final winners in Stage 2. We used auto-eval for Stage 1, and selected top teams with auto-eval in Stage 2 to conduct manual evaluation.</p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A1.SS3">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">A.3 </span>Evaluating straightforward RAG solutions</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS3.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS3.p1.1">We send each CRAG question in a prompt shown below. This prompt is designed to include the original <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS3.p1.1.1">Query Time</span> for the question and ask the LLM to answer the question <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS3.p1.1.2">based on the query time and the retrieved result</span>. Note that the retrieved result was also from the same <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS3.p1.1.3">query time</span> and was provided in CRAG. Moreover, this prompt encourages brief answers and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS3.p1.1.4">“I don’t know”</span> answers when confidence is low.</p>
</div>
<section class="ltx_subsubsection" id="A1.SS3.SSS1">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">A.3.1 </span>Prompts used in straightforward RAG solutions</h4>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS3.SSS1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS3.SSS1.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS3.SSS1.p1.1.1">Vanilla LLM.</span>

PROMPT = """
You are given a Question and the time when it was asked in the Pacific Time Zone (PT), referred to as "Query Time". The query time is formatted as "mm/dd/yyyy, hh:mm:ss PT". Your task is to answer the question in as few words as possible.
<br class="ltx_break"/>Please follow these guidelines when formulating your answer:
<br class="ltx_break"/>1. If the question contains a false premise or assumption, answer “invalid question”.
<br class="ltx_break"/>2. If you are uncertain or don’t know the answer, respond with “I don’t know”.
<br class="ltx_break"/>### Question
<br class="ltx_break"/>{query}
<br class="ltx_break"/>### Query Time
<br class="ltx_break"/>{query_time}
<br class="ltx_break"/>### Answer
<br class="ltx_break"/>"""</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS3.SSS1.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS3.SSS1.p2.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS3.SSS1.p2.1.1">RAG with web search results (Task 1).</span>

PROMPT = """
You are given a Question, References and the time when it was asked in the Pacific Time Zone (PT), referred to as "Query Time". The query time is formatted as "mm/dd/yyyy, hh:mm:ss PT". The references may or may not help answer the question. Your task is to answer the question in as few words as possible.
<br class="ltx_break"/>Please follow these guidelines when formulating your answer:
<br class="ltx_break"/>1. If the question contains a false premise or assumption, answer “invalid question”.
<br class="ltx_break"/>2. If you are uncertain or don’t know the answer, respond with “I don’t know”.
<br class="ltx_break"/>### Question
<br class="ltx_break"/>{query}
<br class="ltx_break"/>### Query Time
<br class="ltx_break"/>{query_time}
<br class="ltx_break"/>### References
<br class="ltx_break"/>{references}
<br class="ltx_break"/>### Answer
<br class="ltx_break"/>"""</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS3.SSS1.p3">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS3.SSS1.p3.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS3.SSS1.p3.1.1">RAG with KG and web search results (Tasks 2 and 3).</span>
PROMPT = """
You are given a Question, References and the time when it was asked in the Pacific Time Zone (PT), referred to as "Query Time". The query time is formatted as "mm/dd/yyyy, hh:mm:ss PT". The references may or may not help answer the question. Your task is to answer the question in as few words as possible.
<br class="ltx_break"/>Please follow these guidelines when formulating your answer:
<br class="ltx_break"/>1. If the question contains a false premise or assumption, answer “invalid question”.
<br class="ltx_break"/>2. If you are uncertain or don’t know the answer, respond with “I don’t know”.
<br class="ltx_break"/>### Question
<br class="ltx_break"/>{query}
<br class="ltx_break"/>### Query Time
<br class="ltx_break"/>{query_time}
<br class="ltx_break"/>### References
<br class="ltx_break"/># web
<br class="ltx_break"/>{web_results}
<br class="ltx_break"/># knowledge graph
<br class="ltx_break"/>{kg_response}
<br class="ltx_break"/>### Answer
<br class="ltx_break"/>"""</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS3.SSS1.p4">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS3.SSS1.p4.1"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS3.SSS1.p4.1.1">Query entity extraction.</span>
PROMPT = """
You are an agent that only outputs JSON. You are given a Query and Query Time. Do the following:
<br class="ltx_break"/>
<br class="ltx_break"/>1) Determine the domain the query is about. The domain should be one of the following: "finance", "sports", "music", "movie", "encyclopedia". If none of the domains apply, use "other". Use "domain" as the key in the result json.
<br class="ltx_break"/>
<br class="ltx_break"/>2) Extract structured information from the query. Include different keys into the result json depending on the domains, and put them DIRECTLY in the result json. Here are the rules:
<br class="ltx_break"/>
<br class="ltx_break"/>For ‘encyclopedia’ and ‘other’ queries, these are possible keys:
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘main_entity’: extract the main entity of the query.
<br class="ltx_break"/>
<br class="ltx_break"/>For ‘finance’ queries, these are possible keys:
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘market_identifier’: stock identifiers including individual company names, stock symbols.
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘metric’: financial metrics that the query is asking about. This must be one of the following: ‘price’, ‘dividend’, ‘P/E ratio’, ‘EPS’, ‘marketCap’, and ‘other’.
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘datetime’: time frame that the query asks about. When datetime is not explicitly mentioned, use ‘Query Time’ as default.
<br class="ltx_break"/>
<br class="ltx_break"/>For ‘movie’ queries, these are possible keys:
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘movie_name’: name of the movie
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘movie_aspect’: if the query is about a movie, which movie aspect the query asks. This must be one of the following: ‘budget’, ‘genres’, ‘original_language’, ‘original_title’, ‘release_date’, ‘revenue’, ‘title’, ‘cast’, ‘crew’, ‘rating’, ‘length’.
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘person’: person name related to moves
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘person_aspect’: if the query is about a person, which person aspect the query asks. This must be one of the following: ‘acted_movies’, ‘directed_movies’, ‘oscar_awards’, ‘birthday’.
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘year’: if the query is about movies released in a specific year, extract the year
<br class="ltx_break"/>
<br class="ltx_break"/>For ‘music’ queries, these are possible keys:
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘artist_name’: name of the artist
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘artist_aspect’: if the query is about an artist, extract the aspect of the artist. This must be one of the following: ‘member’, ‘birth place’, ‘birth date’, ‘lifespan’, ‘artist work’, ‘grammy award count’, ‘grammy award date’.
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘song_name’: name of the song
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘song_aspect’: if the query is about a song, extract the aspect of the song. This must be one of the following: ‘author’, ‘grammy award count’, ‘release country’, ‘release date’.
<br class="ltx_break"/>
<br class="ltx_break"/>For ‘sports’ queries, these are possible keys:
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘sport_type’: one of ‘basketball‘, ‘soccer‘, ‘other‘
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘tournament’: NBA, World Cup, Olympic.
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘team’: teams that users are interested in.
<br class="ltx_break"/>- ‘datetime’: time frame that the user is interested in. When datetime is not explicitly mentioned, use ‘Query Time’ as default.
<br class="ltx_break"/>
<br class="ltx_break"/>Return the results in a FLAT json.
<br class="ltx_break"/>
<br class="ltx_break"/>*NEVER include ANY EXPLANATION or NOTE in the output, ONLY OUTPUT JSON!!!*
<br class="ltx_break"/>"""</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsubsection" id="A1.SS3.SSS2">

<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A1.SS4">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">A.4 </span>Evaluating state-of-the-art industry solutions</h3>
<section class="ltx_subsubsection" id="A1.SS4.SSS1">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">A.4.1 </span>Quality</h4>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.5">We send the CRAG public test set question as input to each of the SOTA RAG systems and collect the responses for human grading. Note that the original <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.5.5">Query Time</span> and the provided retrieval results in CRAG are <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_bold" id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.5.6">not</span> used in this setting. We simply test the questions and ask human graders to grade the responses based on when the query was made to the SOTA system. We called Copilot Pro, Gemini Advanced, and ChatGPT Plus through their web interfaces and Perplexity.ai through its API. <span class="ltx_text" id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.5.7" style="color:#000000;">Meta SG, designed as a smart glasses (SG) assistant, includes default on-device components such as Automatic Speech Recognition (ASR) and Text-to-Speech (TTS), which are not typically enabled by default in other systems. To ensure a fair comparison, we excluded these on-device components, ensuring that answer quality was not affected.</span> <span class="ltx_text" id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.4.4" style="color:#000000;">We called each system on the following dates in Pacific Time: 05/12/2024<math alttext="\sim" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.1.1.m1.1"><semantics id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.1.1.m1.1a"><mo id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.1.1.m1.1.1" mathcolor="#000000" xref="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.1.1.m1.1.1.cmml">∼</mo><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.1.1.m1.1b"><csymbol cd="latexml" (ChatGPT Plus), 05/15/2024<math alttext="\sim" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.4.4.m4.1"><semantics id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.4.4.m4.1a"><mo id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.4.4.m4.1.1" We select <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.5.8">GPT-4o</span> and <span class="ltx_text ltx_font_typewriter" id="A1.SS4.SSS1.p1.5.9">llama-3-sonar-large-32k-online</span> as the base LLM when calling ChatGPT Plus and Perplexity.ai, respectively.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsubsection" id="A1.SS4.SSS2">
<h4 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsubsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsubsection">A.4.2 </span>Latency</h4>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS4.SSS2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS4.SSS2.p1.1">We quantified the latency by calculating the time difference between the timestamp of the query submission to the system and the timestamp when the complete response was received.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS4.SSS2.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS4.SSS2.p2.1"><span class="ltx_text" id="A1.SS4.SSS2.p2.1.1" style="color:#000000;">The latency of Perplexity.ai measured via API call is 2,455ms. Since latency measured by API call and web interface interactions are not directly comparable, we further called Perplexity.ai through its web interface and reported the latency under this setting in Table <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2406.04744v2#S5.T6" title="Table 6 ‣ 5.2 State-of-the-art industry solutions ‣ 5 Benchmarking ‣ CRAG – Comprehensive RAG Benchmark"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">6</span></a>. Note that this latency may not correspond to the accuracy numbers from the API calls.</span> <span class="ltx_text" id="A1.SS4.SSS2.p2.1.2" style="color:#000000;">For Meta SG, we estimated a latency comparable to other web interface interactions by excluding on-device components such as ASR and TTS from the overall end-to-end latency measurement.</span></p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="A1.SS5">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">A.5 </span>Limitations</h3>
<div class="ltx_para ltx_noindent" id="A1.SS5.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="A1.SS5.p1.1"><span class="ltx_text" id="A1.SS5.p1.1.1" style="color:#000000;">The three tasks in our benchmark do not directly evaluate the construction of a first-stage retrieval candidate pool, a demanding retrieval task in its own right. This design decision ensures that the competition remains both challenging and achievable within the KDD Cup’s required three-month timeframe. Despite the limitation, users of our dataset have the option to use the union of all 220K web pages as a corpus to build a retriever. While this corpus does not match the entire web, it allows for fair comparisons and manageable costs.</span></p>
</div>
</section>
</section>
</article>
